[?1049h[?1h=CAT(1)                       General Commands Manual                      CAT(1)

[1mNAME[0m
     [1mcat[0m ‚Äì concatenate and print files

[1mSYNOPSIS[0m
     [1mcat[0m [[1m-belnstuv[0m] [[4mfile[24m [4m...[24m]

[1mDESCRIPTION[0m
     The [1mcat[0m utility reads files sequentially, writing them to the standard
     output.  The [4mfile[24m operands are processed in command-line order.  If [4mfile[24m is
     a single dash (‚Äò[1m-[0m‚Äô) or absent, [1mcat[0m reads from the standard input.  If [4mfile[24m
     is a UNIX domain socket, [1mcat[0m connects to it and then reads it until EOF.
     This complements the UNIX domain binding capability available in inetd(8).

     The options are as follows:

     [1m-b[0m      Number the non-blank output lines, starting at 1.

     [1m-e[0m      Display non-printing characters (see the [1m-v[0m option), and display a
             dollar sign (‚Äò$‚Äô) at the end of each line.

     [1m-l[0m      Set an exclusive advisory lock on the standard output file
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             descriptor.  This lock is set using fcntl(2) with the F_SETLKW
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             command.  If the output file is already locked, [1mcat[0m will block
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             until the lock is acquired.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-n[0m      Number the output lines, starting at 1.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-s[0m      Squeeze multiple adjacent empty lines, causing the output to be
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             single spaced.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-t[0m      Display non-printing characters (see the [1m-v[0m option), and display
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             tab characters as ‚Äò^I‚Äô.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-u[0m      Disable output buffering.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-v[0m      Display non-printing characters so they are visible.  Control
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             characters print as ‚Äò^X‚Äô for control-X; the delete character (octal
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             0177) prints as ‚Äò^?‚Äô.  Non-ASCII characters (with the high bit set)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             are printed as ‚ÄòM-‚Äô (for meta) followed by the character for the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             low 7 bits.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mEXIT[0m [1mSTATUS[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1mcat[0m utility exits¬†0 on success, and¬†>0 if an error occurs.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mEXAMPLES[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The command:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           cat file1
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     will print the contents of [4mfile1[24m to the standard output.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The command:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           cat file1 file2 > file3
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     will sequentially print the contents of [4mfile1[24m and [4mfile2[24m to the file [4mfile3[24m,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     truncating [4mfile3[24m if it already exists.  See the manual page for your shell
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     (e.g., sh(1)) for more information on redirection.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The command:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           cat file1 - file2 - file3
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     will print the contents of [4mfile1[24m, print data it receives from the standard
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     input until it receives an EOF (‚Äò^D‚Äô) character, print the contents of
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [4mfile2[24m, read and output contents of the standard input again, then finally
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     output the contents of [4mfile3[24m.  Note that if the standard input referred to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     a file, the second dash on the command-line would have no effect, since the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     entire contents of the file would have already been read and printed by [1mcat[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     when it encountered the first ‚Äò[1m-[0m‚Äô operand.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mSEE[0m [1mALSO[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     head(1), more(1), pr(1), sh(1), tail(1), vis(1), zcat(1), fcntl(2),
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     setbuf(3)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Rob Pike, ‚ÄúUNIX Style, or cat -v Considered Harmful‚Äù, [4mUSENIX[24m [4mSummer[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [4mConference[24m [4mProceedings[24m, 1983.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mSTANDARDS[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1mcat[0m utility is compliant with the IEEE Std 1003.2-1992 (‚ÄúPOSIX.2‚Äù)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     specification.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The flags [[1m-belnstv[0m] are extensions to the specification.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mHISTORY[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     A [1mcat[0m utility appeared in Version¬†1 AT&T UNIX.  Dennis Ritchie designed and
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     wrote the first man page.  It appears to have been for [1mcat[0m.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mBUGS[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Because of the shell language mechanism used to perform output redirection,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     the command ‚Äúcat file1 file2 > file1‚Äù will cause the original data in [4mfile1[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     to be destroyed!
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1mcat[0m utility does not recognize multibyte characters when the [1m-t[0m or [1m-v[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     option is in effect.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K

[?1049h[?1h=CMP(1)                            User Commands                           CMP(1)

[1mNAME[0m
       cmp - compare two files byte by byte

[1mSYNOPSIS[0m
       [1mcmp[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [4mFILE1[24m [[4mFILE2[24m [[4mSKIP1[24m [[4mSKIP2[24m]]]

[1mDESCRIPTION[0m
       Compare two files byte by byte.

       [1m-b[0m  [1m--print-bytes[0m
              Print differing bytes.

       [1m-i[0m SKIP  [1m--ignore-initial[0m=[4mSKIP[24m
              Skip the first SKIP bytes of input.

       [1m-i[0m SKIP1:SKIP2  [1m--ignore-initial[0m=[4mSKIP1[24m:SKIP2

              Skip the first SKIP1 bytes of FILE1 and the first SKIP2 bytes of
              FILE2.

       [1m-l[0m  [1m--verbose[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              Output byte numbers and values of all differing bytes.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1m-n[0m LIMIT  [1m--bytes[0m=[4mLIMIT[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              Compare at most LIMIT bytes.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1m-s[0m  [1m--quiet[0m  [1m--silent[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              Output nothing; yield exit status only.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1m-v[0m  [1m--version[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              Output version info.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1m--help[0m Output this help.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       SKIP1 and SKIP2 are the number of bytes to skip in each file.  SKIP
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       values may be followed by the following multiplicative suffixes: kB 1000,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       K 1024, MB 1,000,000, M 1,048,576, GB 1,000,000,000, G 1,073,741,824, and
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       so on for T, P, E, Z, Y.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       If a FILE is `-' or missing, read standard input.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K

[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM

[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM       [1m-s[0m  [1m--quiet[0m  [1m--silent[0m

[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM       [1m-n[0m LIMIT  [1m--bytes[0m=[4mLIMIT[24m
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              Output byte numbers and values of all differing bytes.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM       [1m-l[0m  [1m--verbose[0m
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              FILE2.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              Skip the first SKIP1 bytes of FILE1 and the first SKIP2 bytes of
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM       [1m-i[0m SKIP1:SKIP2  [1m--ignore-initial[0m=[4mSKIP1[24m:SKIP2

[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM       [1m-i[0m SKIP  [1m--ignore-initial[0m=[4mSKIP[24m

[?1049h[?1h=DU(1)                        General Commands Manual                       DU(1)

[1mNAME[0m
     [1mdu[0m ‚Äì display disk usage statistics

[1mSYNOPSIS[0m
     [1mdu[0m [[1m-Aclnx[0m] [[1m-H[0m | [1m-L[0m | [1m-P[0m] [[1m-g[0m | [1m-h[0m | [1m-k[0m | [1m-m[0m] [[1m-a[0m | [1m-s[0m | [1m-d[0m [4mdepth[24m]
        [[1m-B[0m [4mblocksize[24m] [[1m-I[0m [4mmask[24m] [[1m-t[0m [4mthreshold[24m] [[4mfile[24m [4m...[24m]

[1mDESCRIPTION[0m
     The [1mdu[0m utility displays the file system block usage for each file argument
     and for each directory in the file hierarchy rooted in each directory
     argument.  If no file is specified, the block usage of the hierarchy rooted
     in the current directory is displayed.

     The options are as follows:

     [1m-A[0m      Display the apparent size instead of the disk usage.  This can be
             helpful when operating on compressed volumes or sparse files.

     [1m-B[0m [4mblocksize[24m
             Calculate block counts in [4mblocksize[24m byte blocks.  This is different
             from the [1m-h[0m, [1m-k[0m, [1m-m[0m, [1m--si[0m and [1m-g[0m options or setting BLOCKSIZE and
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             gives an estimate of how much space the examined file hierarchy
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             would require on a filesystem with the given [4mblocksize[24m.  Unless in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1m-A[0m mode, [4mblocksize[24m is rounded up to the next multiple of 512.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-H[0m      Symbolic links on the command line are followed, symbolic links in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             file hierarchies are not followed.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-I[0m [4mmask[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Ignore files and directories matching the specified [4mmask[24m.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-L[0m      Symbolic links on the command line and in file hierarchies are
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             followed.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-P[0m      No symbolic links are followed.  This is the default.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-a[0m      Display an entry for each file in a file hierarchy.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-c[0m      Display a grand total.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-d[0m [4mdepth[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Display an entry for all files and directories [4mdepth[24m directories
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             deep.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-g[0m      Display block counts in 1073741824-byte (1 GiB) blocks.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-h[0m      ‚ÄúHuman-readable‚Äù output.  Use unit suffixes: Byte, Kilobyte,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Megabyte, Gigabyte, Terabyte and Petabyte based on powers of 1024.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-k[0m      Display block counts in 1024-byte (1 kiB) blocks.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-l[0m      If a file has multiple hard links, count its size multiple times.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             The default behavior of [1mdu[0m is to count files with multiple hard
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             links only once.  When the [1m-l[0m option is specified, the hard link
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             checks are disabled, and these files are counted (and displayed) as
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     [1m-L[0m      Symbolic links on the command line and in file hierarchies are
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM             Ignore files and directories matching the specified [4mmask[24m.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     [1m-I[0m [4mmask[24m
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM             file hierarchies are not followed.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     [1m-H[0m      Symbolic links on the command line are followed, symbolic links in
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM             [1m-A[0m mode, [4mblocksize[24m is rounded up to the next multiple of 512.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM             would require on a filesystem with the given [4mblocksize[24m.  Unless in
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM             gives an estimate of how much space the examined file hierarchy
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM             from the [1m-h[0m, [1m-k[0m, [1m-m[0m, [1m--si[0m and [1m-g[0m options or setting BLOCKSIZE and
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM             Calculate block counts in [4mblocksize[24m byte blocks.  This is different
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     [1m-B[0m [4mblocksize[24m
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM             helpful when operating on compressed volumes or sparse files.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     [1m-A[0m      Display the apparent size instead of the disk usage.  This can be
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     The options are as follows:
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     in the current directory is displayed.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     argument.  If no file is specified, the block usage of the hierarchy rooted
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     and for each directory in the file hierarchy rooted in each directory
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     The [1mdu[0m utility displays the file system block usage for each file argument
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM[1mDESCRIPTION[0m
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM        [[1m-B[0m [4mblocksize[24m] [[1m-I[0m [4mmask[24m] [[1m-t[0m [4mthreshold[24m] [[4mfile[24m [4m...[24m]
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     [1mdu[0m [[1m-Aclnx[0m] [[1m-H[0m | [1m-L[0m | [1m-P[0m] [[1m-g[0m | [1m-h[0m | [1m-k[0m | [1m-m[0m] [[1m-a[0m | [1m-s[0m | [1m-d[0m [4mdepth[24m]
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM[1mSYNOPSIS[0m

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             would require on a filesystem with the given [4mblocksize[24m.  Unless in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1m-A[0m mode, [4mblocksize[24m is rounded up to the next multiple of 512.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-H[0m      Symbolic links on the command line are followed, symbolic links in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             file hierarchies are not followed.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-I[0m [4mmask[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Ignore files and directories matching the specified [4mmask[24m.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-L[0m      Symbolic links on the command line and in file hierarchies are
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             followed.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-P[0m      No symbolic links are followed.  This is the default.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-a[0m      Display an entry for each file in a file hierarchy.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-c[0m      Display a grand total.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-d[0m [4mdepth[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Display an entry for all files and directories [4mdepth[24m directories
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             deep.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-g[0m      Display block counts in 1073741824-byte (1 GiB) blocks.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-h[0m      ‚ÄúHuman-readable‚Äù output.  Use unit suffixes: Byte, Kilobyte,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Megabyte, Gigabyte, Terabyte and Petabyte based on powers of 1024.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-k[0m      Display block counts in 1024-byte (1 kiB) blocks.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-l[0m      If a file has multiple hard links, count its size multiple times.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             The default behavior of [1mdu[0m is to count files with multiple hard
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             links only once.  When the [1m-l[0m option is specified, the hard link
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             checks are disabled, and these files are counted (and displayed) as
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             many times as they are found.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-m[0m      Display block counts in 1048576-byte (1 MiB) blocks.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-n[0m      Ignore files and directories with user ‚Äúnodump‚Äù flag (UF_NODUMP)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             set.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-r[0m      Generate messages about directories that cannot be read, files that
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             cannot be opened, and so on.  This is the default case.  This
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             option exists solely for conformance with X/Open Portability Guide
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Issue¬†4 (‚ÄúXPG4‚Äù).

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Megabyte, Gigabyte, Terabyte and Petabyte based on powers of 1000.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [4mthreshold[24m is negative, display only entries for which size is less

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-x[0m      File system mount points are not traversed.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1mdu[0m utility counts the storage used by symbolic links and not the files

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     each other and the command's actions are determined by the last one

[?1049h[?1h=LS(1)                        General Commands Manual                       LS(1)

[1mNAME[0m
     [1mls[0m ‚Äì list directory contents

[1mSYNOPSIS[0m
     [1mls[0m [[1m-@ABCFGHILOPRSTUWabcdefghiklmnopqrstuvwxy1%,[0m] [[1m--color[0m=[4mwhen[24m]
        [[1m-D[0m [4mformat[24m] [[4mfile[24m [4m...[24m]

[1mDESCRIPTION[0m
     For each operand that names a [4mfile[24m of a type other than directory, [1mls[0m
     displays its name as well as any requested, associated information.  For
     each operand that names a [4mfile[24m of type directory, [1mls[0m displays the names of
     files contained within that directory, as well as any requested, associated
     information.

     If no operands are given, the contents of the current directory are
     displayed.  If more than one operand is given, non-directory operands are
     displayed first; directory and non-directory operands are sorted separately
     and in lexicographical order.

     The following options are available:

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-@[0m      Display extended attribute keys and sizes in long ([1m-l[0m) output.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-A[0m      Include directory entries whose names begin with a dot (‚Äò[4m.[24m‚Äô) except
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             for [4m.[24m and [4m..[24m.  Automatically set for the super-user unless [1m-I[0m is

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-A[0m      Include directory entries whose names begin with a dot (‚Äò[4m.[24m‚Äô) except

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             and current locale settings) in file names as \[4mxxx[24m, where [4mxxx[24m is

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             defined in IEEE Std 1003.1-2008 (‚ÄúPOSIX.1‚Äù).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-C[0m      Force multi-column output; this is the default when output is to a
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             terminal.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             When printing in the long ([1m-l[0m) format, use [4mformat[24m to format the

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-F[0m      Display a slash (‚Äò/‚Äô) immediately after each pathname that is a

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             vertical bar (‚Äò|‚Äô) after each that is a FIFO.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-G[0m      Enable colorized output.  This option is equivalent to defining
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             CLICOLOR or COLORTERM in the environment and setting [1m--color[0m=[4mauto[24m.

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-H[0m      Symbolic links on the command line are followed.  This option is

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-I[0m      Prevent [1m-A[0m from being automatically set for the super-user.  This
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             option is not defined in IEEE Std 1003.1-2008 (‚ÄúPOSIX.1‚Äù).

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1malways[0m will make [1mls[0m always output color.  If TERM is unset or set
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             to an invalid terminal, then [1mls[0m will fall back to explicit ANSI

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-h[0m      When used with the [1m-l[0m option, use unit suffixes: Byte, Kilobyte,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Megabyte, Gigabyte, Terabyte and Petabyte in order to reduce the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             number of digits to four or fewer using base 2 for sizes.  This
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             option is not defined in IEEE Std 1003.1-2008 (‚ÄúPOSIX.1‚Äù).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-i[0m      For each file, print the file's file serial number (inode number).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-k[0m      This has the same effect as setting environment variable BLOCKSIZE
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             to 1024, except that it also nullifies any [1m-h[0m options to its left.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-l[0m      (The lowercase letter ‚Äúell‚Äù.) List files in the long format, as
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             described in the [4mThe[24m [4mLong[24m [4mFormat[24m subsection below.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-m[0m      Stream output format; list files across the page, separated by
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             commas.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-n[0m      Display user and group IDs numerically rather than converting to a
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             user or group name in a long ([1m-l[0m) output.  This option turns on the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1m-l[0m option.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-o[0m      List in long format, but omit the group id.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-p[0m      Write a slash (‚Äò/‚Äô) after each filename if that file is a
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             directory.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-q[0m      Force printing of non-graphic characters in file names as the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             character ‚Äò?‚Äô; this is the default when output is to a terminal.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-r[0m      Reverse the order of the sort.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-s[0m      Display the number of blocks used in the file system by each file.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Block sizes and directory totals are handled as described in [4mThe[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [4mLong[24m [4mFormat[24m subsection below, except (if the long format is not
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             also requested) the directory totals are not output when the output
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             is in a single column, even if multi-column output is requested.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             ([1m-l[0m) format, display complete time information for the file,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             including month, day, hour, minute, second, and year.  The [1m-D[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             option gives even more control over the output format.  This option
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             is not defined in IEEE Std 1003.1-2008 (‚ÄúPOSIX.1‚Äù).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-t[0m      Sort by descending time modified (most recently modified first).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             If two files have the same modification timestamp, sort their names
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             in ascending lexicographical order.  The [1m-r[0m option reverses both of
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             these sort orders.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Note that these sort orders are contradictory: the time sequence is
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             in descending order, the lexicographical sort is in ascending
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             order.  This behavior is mandated by IEEE Std 1003.2 (‚ÄúPOSIX.2‚Äù).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             This feature can cause problems listing files stored with
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             sequential names on FAT file systems, such as from digital cameras,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             where it is possible to have more than one image with the same
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             timestamp.  In such a case, the photos cannot be listed in the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             sequence in which they were taken.  To ensure the same sort order
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             for time and for lexicographical sorting, set the environment
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             variable LS_SAMESORT or use the [1m-y[0m option.  This causes [1mls[0m to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             reverse the lexicographical sort order when sorting files with the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             same modification timestamp.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-u[0m      Use time of last access, instead of time of last modification of
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             the file for sorting ([1m-t[0m) or long printing ([1m-l[0m).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-v[0m      Force unedited printing of non-graphic characters; this is the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             default when output is not to a terminal.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-w[0m      Force raw printing of non-printable characters.  This is the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             default when output is not to a terminal.  This option is not
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             defined in IEEE Std 1003.1-2001 (‚ÄúPOSIX.1‚Äù).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-x[0m      The same as [1m-C[0m, except that the multi-column output is produced
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             with entries sorted across, rather than down, the columns.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-y[0m      When the [1m-t[0m option is set, sort the alphabetical output in the same
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             order as the time output.  This has the same effect as setting
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             LS_SAMESORT.  See the description of the [1m-t[0m option for more
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             details.  This option is not defined in IEEE Std 1003.1-2001
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             (‚ÄúPOSIX.1‚Äù).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-%[0m      Distinguish dataless files and directories with a '%' character in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             long
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-1[0m      (The numeric digit ‚Äúone‚Äù.) Force output to be one entry per line.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             This is the default when output is not to a terminal.  ([1m-l[0m) output,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             and don't materialize dataless directories when listing them.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-[0m,      (Comma) When the [1m-l[0m option is set, print file sizes grouped and
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             separated by thousands using the non-monetary separator returned by
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             localeconv(3), typically a comma or period.  If no locale is set,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             or the locale does not have a non-monetary separator, this option
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             has no effect.  This option is not defined in IEEE Std 1003.1-2001
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             (‚ÄúPOSIX.1‚Äù).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1m-1[0m, [1m-C[0m, [1m-x[0m, and [1m-l[0m options all override each other; the last one
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     specified determines the format used.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1m-c[0m, [1m-u[0m, and [1m-U[0m options all override each other; the last one specified
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     determines the file time used.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1m-S[0m and [1m-t[0m options override each other; the last one specified
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     determines the sort order used.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1m-B[0m, [1m-b[0m, [1m-w[0m, and [1m-q[0m options all override each other; the last one
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     specified determines the format used for non-printable characters.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1m-H[0m, [1m-L[0m and [1m-P[0m options all override each other (either partially or
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     fully); they are applied in the order specified.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     By default, [1mls[0m lists one entry per line to standard output; the exceptions
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     are to terminals or when the [1m-C[0m or [1m-x[0m options are specified.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     File information is displayed with one or more ‚ü®blank‚ü©s separating the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     information associated with the [1m-i[0m, [1m-s[0m, and [1m-l[0m options.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K   [1mThe[0m [1mLong[0m [1mFormat[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     If the [1m-l[0m option is given, the following information is displayed for each
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     file: file mode, number of links, owner name, group name, number of bytes
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     in the file, abbreviated month, day-of-month file was last modified, hour
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     file last modified, minute file last modified, and the pathname.  If the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     file or directory has extended attributes, the permissions field printed by
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     the [1m-l[0m option is followed by a '@' character.  Otherwise, if the file or
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     directory has extended security information (such as an access control
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     list), the permissions field printed by the [1m-l[0m option is followed by a '+'
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     character.  If the [1m-%[0m option is given, a '%' character follows the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     permissions field for dataless files and directories, possibly replacing
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     the '@' or '+' character.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     If the modification time of the file is more than 6 months in the past or
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     future, and the [1m-D[0m or [1m-T[0m are not specified, then the year of the last
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     modification is displayed in place of the hour and minute fields.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     If the owner or group names are not a known user or group name, or the [1m-n[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     option is given, the numeric ID's are displayed.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     If the file is a character special or block special file, the device number
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     for the file is displayed in the size field.  If the file is a symbolic
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     link the pathname of the linked-to file is preceded by ‚Äú->‚Äù.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The listing of a directory's contents is preceded by a labeled total number
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     of blocks used in the file system by the files which are listed as the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     directory's contents (which may or may not include [4m.[24m and [4m..[24m and other files
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     which start with a dot, depending on other options).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     file last modified, minute file last modified, and the pathname.  If the
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     in the file, abbreviated month, day-of-month file was last modified, hour
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     file: file mode, number of links, owner name, group name, number of bytes
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     If the [1m-l[0m option is given, the following information is displayed for each
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM   [1mThe[0m [1mLong[0m [1mFormat[0m
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     information associated with the [1m-i[0m, [1m-s[0m, and [1m-l[0m options.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     File information is displayed with one or more ‚ü®blank‚ü©s separating the
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     are to terminals or when the [1m-C[0m or [1m-x[0m options are specified.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     By default, [1mls[0m lists one entry per line to standard output; the exceptions
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     If the owner or group names are not a known user or group name, or the [1m-n[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     option is given, the numeric ID's are displayed.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     If the file is a character special or block special file, the device number
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     for the file is displayed in the size field.  If the file is a symbolic
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     link the pathname of the linked-to file is preceded by ‚Äú->‚Äù.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The listing of a directory's contents is preceded by a labeled total number
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     of blocks used in the file system by the files which are listed as the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     directory's contents (which may or may not include [4m.[24m and [4m..[24m and other files
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     which start with a dot, depending on other options).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The default block size is 512 bytes.  The block size may be set with option
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-k[0m or environment variable BLOCKSIZE.  Numbers of blocks in the output will
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     have been rounded up so the numbers of bytes is at least as many as used by
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     the corresponding file system blocks (which might have a different size).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The file mode printed under the [1m-l[0m option consists of the entry type and
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     the permissions.  The entry type character describes the type of file, as
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     follows:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           [1m-[0m     Regular file.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           [1mb[0m     Block special file.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           [1mc[0m     Character special file.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           [1md[0m     Directory.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           [1ml[0m     Symbolic link.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           [1mp[0m     FIFO.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           [1ms[0m     Socket.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           [1mw[0m     Whiteout.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The next three fields are three characters each: owner permissions, group
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     permissions, and other permissions.  Each field has three character
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     positions:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           1.   If [1mr[0m, the file is readable; if [1m-[0m, it is not readable.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           2.   If [1mw[0m, the file is writable; if [1m-[0m, it is not writable.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           3.   The first of the following that applies:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                      [1mS[0m     If in the owner permissions, the file is not
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            executable and set-user-ID mode is set.  If in the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            group permissions, the file is not executable and
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            set-group-ID mode is set.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                      [1ms[0m     If in the owner permissions, the file is executable
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            and set-user-ID mode is set.  If in the group
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            permissions, the file is executable and setgroup-ID
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            mode is set.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                      [1mx[0m     The file is executable or the directory is
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            searchable.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                      [1m-[0m     The file is neither readable, writable, executable,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            nor set-user-ID nor set-group-ID mode, nor sticky.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            (See below.)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     positions:
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     permissions, and other permissions.  Each field has three character
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     The next three fields are three characters each: owner permissions, group
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           [1mw[0m     Whiteout.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           [1ms[0m     Socket.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           [1mp[0m     FIFO.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           [1ml[0m     Symbolic link.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           [1md[0m     Directory.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           [1mc[0m     Character special file.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           [1mb[0m     Block special file.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                      [1ms[0m     If in the owner permissions, the file is executable
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            and set-user-ID mode is set.  If in the group
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            permissions, the file is executable and setgroup-ID
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            mode is set.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                      [1mx[0m     The file is executable or the directory is
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            searchable.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                      [1m-[0m     The file is neither readable, writable, executable,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            nor set-user-ID nor set-group-ID mode, nor sticky.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            (See below.)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                These next two apply only to the third character in the last
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                group (other permissions).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                      [1mT[0m     The sticky bit is set (mode 1000), but not execute
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            or search permission.  (See chmod(1) or sticky(7).)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                      [1mt[0m     The sticky bit is set (mode 1000), and is searchable
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                            or executable.  (See chmod(1) or sticky(7).)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The next field contains a plus (‚Äò+‚Äô) character if the file has an ACL, or a
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     space (‚Äò ‚Äô) if it does not.  The [1mls[0m utility does not show the actual ACL;
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     use getfacl(1) to do this.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mENVIRONMENT[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The following environment variables affect the execution of [1mls[0m:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     BLOCKSIZE           If this is set, its value, rounded up to 512 or down to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         a multiple of 512, will be used as the block size in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         bytes by the [1m-l[0m and [1m-s[0m options.  See [4mThe[24m [4mLong[24m [4mFormat[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         subsection for more information.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     CLICOLOR            Use ANSI color sequences to distinguish file types.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         See LSCOLORS below.  In addition to the file types
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         mentioned in the [1m-F[0m option some extra attributes
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         (setuid bit set, etc.) are also displayed.  The
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         colorization is dependent on a terminal type with the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         proper termcap(5) capabilities.  The default ‚Äúcons25‚Äù
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         console has the proper capabilities, but to display the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         colors in an xterm(1), for example, the TERM variable
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         must be set to ‚Äúxterm-color‚Äù.  Other terminal types may
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         require similar adjustments.  Colorization is silently
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         disabled if the output is not directed to a terminal
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         unless the CLICOLOR_FORCE variable is defined or
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         [1m--color[0m is set to ‚Äúalways‚Äù.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     CLICOLOR_FORCE      Color sequences are normally disabled if the output is
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         not directed to a terminal.  This can be overridden by
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         setting this variable.  The TERM variable still needs
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         to reference a color capable terminal however otherwise
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         it is not possible to determine which color sequences
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         to use.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     COLORTERM           See description for CLICOLOR above.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     COLUMNS             If this variable contains a string representing a
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         decimal integer, it is used as the column position
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         width for displaying multiple-text-column output.  The
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         [1mls[0m utility calculates how many pathname text columns to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         display based on the width provided.  (See [1m-C[0m and [1m-x[0m.)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     LANG                The locale to use when determining the order of day and
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         month in the long [1m-l[0m format output.  See environ(7) for
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         more information.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     LSCOLORS            The value of this variable describes what color to use
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         for which attribute when colors are enabled with
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         CLICOLOR or COLORTERM.  This string is a concatenation
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         of pairs of the format [4mfb[24m, where [4mf[24m is the foreground
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         color and [4mb[24m is the background color.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         The color designators are as follows:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1ma[0m     black
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mb[0m     red
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mc[0m     green
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1md[0m     brown
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1me[0m     blue
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mf[0m     magenta
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mg[0m     cyan
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mh[0m     light grey
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mA[0m     bold black, usually shows up as dark grey
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mB[0m     bold red
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mC[0m     bold green
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mD[0m     bold brown, usually shows up as yellow
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mE[0m     bold blue
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mF[0m     bold magenta
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mG[0m     bold cyan
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mH[0m     bold light grey; looks like bright white
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               [1mx[0m     default foreground or background
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         Note that the above are standard ANSI colors.  The
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         actual display may differ depending on the color
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         capabilities of the terminal in use.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         The order of the attributes are as follows:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               1.   directory
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               2.   symbolic link
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               3.   socket
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               4.   pipe
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               5.   executable
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               6.   block special
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               7.   character special
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               8.   executable with setuid bit set
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               9.   executable with setgid bit set
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               10.  directory writable to others, with sticky
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                                    bit
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                               11.  directory writable to others, without sticky
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                                    bit
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         The default is "exfxcxdxbxegedabagacad", i.e., blue
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         foreground and default background for regular
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         directories, black foreground and red background for
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         setuid executables, etc.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     LS_COLWIDTHS        If this variable is set, it is considered to be a
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         colon-delimited list of minimum column widths.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         Unreasonable and insufficient widths are ignored (thus
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         zero signifies a dynamically sized column).  Not all
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         columns have changeable widths.  The fields are, in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         order: inode, block count, number of links, user name,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         group name, flags, file size, file name.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     LS_SAMESORT         If this variable is set, the [1m-t[0m option sorts the names
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         of files with the same modification timestamp in the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         same sense as the time sort.  See the description of
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         the [1m-t[0m option for more details.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     TERM                The CLICOLOR and COLORTERM functionality depends on a
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         terminal type with color capabilities.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     TZ                  The timezone to use when displaying dates.  See
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                         environ(7) for more information.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mEXIT[0m [1mSTATUS[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1mls[0m utility exits¬†0 on success, and¬†>0 if an error occurs.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mEXAMPLES[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     List the contents of the current working directory in long format:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           $ ls -l
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     In addition to listing the contents of the current working directory in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     long format, show inode numbers, file flags (see chflags(1)), and suffix
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     each filename with a symbol representing its file type:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           $ ls -lioF
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     List the files in [4m/var/log[24m, sorting the output such that the most recently
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     modified entries are printed first:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           $ ls -lt /var/log
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mCOMPATIBILITY[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The group field is now automatically included in the long listing for files
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     in order to be compatible with the IEEE Std 1003.2 (‚ÄúPOSIX.2‚Äù)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     specification.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mLEGACY[0m [1mDESCRIPTION[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     In legacy mode, the [1m-f[0m option does not turn on the [1m-a[0m option and the [1m-g[0m,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-n[0m, and [1m-o[0m options do not turn on the [1m-l[0m option.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Also, the [1m-o[0m option causes the file flags to be included in a long (-l)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     output; there is no [1m-O[0m option.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     When [1m-H[0m is specified (and not overridden by [1m-L[0m or [1m-P[0m) and a file argument
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     is a symlink that resolves to a non-directory file, the output will reflect
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     the nature of the link, rather than that of the file.  In legacy operation,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     the output will describe the file.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     For more information about legacy mode, see compat(5).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mSEE[0m [1mALSO[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     chflags(1), chmod(1), getfacl(1), sort(1), xterm(1), localeconv(3),
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     strftime(3), strmode(3), compat(5), termcap(5), sticky(7), symlink(7)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mSTANDARDS[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     With the exception of options [1m-g[0m, [1m-n[0m and [1m-o[0m, the [1mls[0m utility conforms to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     IEEE Std 1003.1-2001 (‚ÄúPOSIX.1‚Äù) and IEEE Std 1003.1-2008 (‚ÄúPOSIX.1‚Äù).  The
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     options [1m-B[0m, [1m-D[0m, [1m-G[0m, [1m-I[0m, [1m-T[0m, [1m-U[0m, [1m-W[0m, [1m-Z[0m, [1m-b[0m, [1m-h[0m, [1m-w[0m, [1m-y[0m and [1m-[0m, are non-
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     standard extensions.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The ACL support is compatible with IEEE Std¬†1003.2c (‚ÄúPOSIX.2c‚Äù) Draft¬†17
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     (withdrawn).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mHISTORY[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     An [1mls[0m command appeared in Version¬†1 AT&T UNIX.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mBUGS[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     To maintain backward compatibility, the relationships between the many
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     options are quite complex.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The exception mentioned in the [1m-s[0m option description might be a feature
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     that was based on the fact that single-column output usually goes to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     something other than a terminal.  It is debatable whether this is a design
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     bug.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     IEEE Std 1003.2 (‚ÄúPOSIX.2‚Äù) mandates opposite sort orders for files with
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     the same timestamp when sorting with the [1m-t[0m option.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[KmacOS 12.5                       August 31, 2020                      macOS 12.5

[?1049h[?1h=W(1)                         General Commands Manual                        W(1)

[1mNAME[0m
     [1mw[0m ‚Äì display who is logged in and what they are doing

[1mSYNOPSIS[0m
     [1mw[0m [[1m-hin[0m] [[4muser[24m [4m...[24m]

[1mDESCRIPTION[0m
     The [1mw[0m utility prints a summary of the current activity on the system,
     including what each user is doing.  The first line displays the current
     time of day, how long the system has been running, the number of users
     logged into the system, and the load averages.  The load average numbers
     give the number of jobs in the run queue averaged over 1, 5 and 15 minutes.

     The fields output are the user's login name, the name of the terminal the
     user is on, the host from which the user is logged in, the time the user
     logged on, the time since the user last typed anything, and the name and
     arguments of the current process.

     The options are as follows:

     [1m-h[0m      Suppress the heading.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-i[0m      Output is sorted by idle time.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     If one or more [4muser[24m names are specified, the output is restricted to those
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     users.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mCOMPATIBILITY[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1m-M[0m, [1m-N[0m, [1m-d[0m, [1m-f[0m, [1m-l[0m, [1m-n[0m, [1m-s[0m, and [1m-w[0m flags are no longer supported.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mSEE[0m [1mALSO[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     finger(1), ps(1), uptime(1), who(1)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mHISTORY[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1mw[0m command appeared in 3.0BSD.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mBUGS[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The notion of the ‚Äúcurrent process‚Äù is muddy.  The current algorithm is
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     ``the highest numbered process on the terminal that is not ignoring
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     interrupts, or, if there is none, the highest numbered process on the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     terminal''.  This fails, for example, in critical sections of programs like
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     the shell and editor, or when faulty programs running in the background
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     fork and fail to ignore interrupts.  (In cases where no process can be
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     found, [1mw[0m prints ‚Äú-‚Äù.)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The CPU time is only an estimate, in particular, if someone leaves a
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     background process running after logging out, the person currently on that
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     terminal is ‚Äúcharged‚Äù with the time.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Background processes are not shown, even though they account for much of
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     the load on the system.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Sometimes processes, typically those in the background, are printed with
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     null or garbaged arguments.  In these cases, the name of the command is
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     printed in parentheses.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1mw[0m utility does not know about the new conventions for detection of
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     background jobs.  It will sometimes find a background job instead of the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     right one.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Long hostnames and IPv6 addresses may be truncated; however, the who(1)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     utility will display full hostnames.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[KmacOS 12.5                        June 6, 1993                        macOS 12.5
