[1mNAME[0m
     [1mps[0m ‚Äì process status

[1mSYNOPSIS[0m
     [1mps[0m [[1m-AaCcEefhjlMmrSTvwXx[0m] [[1m-O[0m [4mfmt[24m | [1m-o[0m [4mfmt[24m] [[1m-G[0m [4mgid[24m[,[4mgid...[24m]]
        [[1m-g[0m [4mgrp[24m[,[4mgrp...[24m]] [[1m-u[0m [4muid[24m[,[4muid...[24m]] [[1m-p[0m [4mpid[24m[,[4mpid...[24m]] [[1m-t[0m [4mtty[24m[,[4mtty...[24m]]
        [[1m-U[0m [4muser[24m[,[4muser...[24m]]
     [1mps[0m [[1m-L[0m]

[1mDESCRIPTION[0m
     The [1mps[0m utility displays a header line, followed by lines containing
     information about all of your processes that have controlling terminals.

     A different set of processes can be selected for display by using any
     combination of the [1m-a[0m, [1m-G[0m, [1m-g[0m, [1m-p[0m, [1m-T[0m, [1m-t[0m, [1m-U[0m, and [1m-u[0m options.  If more
     than one of these options are given, then [1mps[0m will select all processes
     which are matched by at least one of the given options.

     For the processes which have been selected for display, [1mps[0m will usually
     display one line per process.  The [1m-M[0m option may result in multiple output
     lines (one line per thread) for some processes.  By default all of these
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     output lines are sorted first by controlling terminal, then by process ID.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1m-m[0m, [1m-r[0m, and [1m-v[0m options will change the sort order.  If more than one
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     sorting option was given, then the selected processes will be sorted by the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     last sorting option which was specified.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     For the processes which have been selected for display, the information to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     display is selected based on a set of keywords (see the [1m-L[0m, [1m-O[0m, and [1m-o[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     options).  The default output format includes, for each process, the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     process' ID, controlling terminal, CPU time (including both user and system
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     time), state, and associated command.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The options are as follows:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-A[0m      Display information about other users' processes, including those
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             without controlling terminals.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-a[0m      Display information about other users' processes as well as your
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             own.  This will skip any processes which do not have a controlling
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             terminal, unless the [1m-x[0m option is also specified.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-C[0m      Change the way the CPU percentage is calculated by using a ‚Äúraw‚Äù
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             CPU calculation that ignores ‚Äúresident‚Äù time (this normally has no
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             effect).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-c[0m      Change the ‚Äúcommand‚Äù column output to just contain the executable
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             name, rather than the full command line.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-d[0m      Like [1m-A[0m, but excludes session leaders.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-E[0m      Display the environment as well.  This does not reflect changes in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             the environment after process launch.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-e[0m      Identical to [1m-A[0m.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-f[0m      Display the uid, pid, parent pid, recent CPU usage, process start
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             time, controlling tty, elapsed CPU usage, and the associated
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             command.  If the [1m-u[0m option is also used, display the user name
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             rather then the numeric uid.  When [1m-o[0m or [1m-O[0m is used to add to the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             display following [1m-f[0m, the command field is not truncated as
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             severely as it is in other formats.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-G[0m      Display information about processes which are running with the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             specified real group IDs.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-g[0m      Display information about processes with the specified process
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             group leaders.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-h[0m      Repeat the information header as often as necessary to guarantee
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             one header per page of information.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-j[0m      Print information associated with the following keywords: [1muser[0m,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1mpid[0m, [1mppid[0m, [1mpgid[0m, [1msess[0m, [1mjobc[0m, [1mstate[0m, [1mtt[0m, [1mtime[0m, and [1mcommand[0m.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-L[0m      List the set of keywords available for the [1m-O[0m and [1m-o[0m options.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-l[0m      Display information associated with the following keywords: [1muid[0m,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1mpid[0m, [1mppid[0m, [1mflags[0m, [1mcpu[0m, [1mpri[0m, [1mnice[0m, [1mvsz=SZ[0m, [1mrss[0m, [1mwchan[0m, [1mstate=S[0m,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1mpaddr=ADDR[0m, [1mtty[0m, [1mtime[0m, and [1mcommand=CMD[0m.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-M[0m      Print the threads corresponding to each task.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-m[0m      Sort by memory usage, instead of the combination of controlling
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             terminal and process ID.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-O[0m      Add the information associated with the space or comma separated
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             list of keywords specified, after the process ID, in the default
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             information display.  Keywords may be appended with an equals (‚Äò=‚Äô)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             sign and a string.  This causes the printed header to use the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             specified string instead of the standard header.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-o[0m      Display information associated with the space or comma separated
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             list of keywords specified.  Multiple keywords may also be given in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             the form of more than one [1m-o[0m option.  Keywords may be appended with
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             an equals (‚Äò=‚Äô) sign and a string.  This causes the printed header
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             to use the specified string instead of the standard header.  If all
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             keywords have empty header texts, no header line is written.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-p[0m      Display information about processes which match the specified
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             process IDs.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-r[0m      Sort by current CPU usage, instead of the combination of
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             controlling terminal and process ID.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-S[0m      Change the way the process time is calculated by summing all exited
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             children to their parent process.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-T[0m      Display information about processes attached to the device
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             associated with the standard input.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-t[0m      Display information about processes attached to the specified
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             terminal devices.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-U[0m      Display the processes belonging to the specified real user IDs.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-u[0m      Display the processes belonging to the specified usernames.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-v[0m      Display information associated with the following keywords: [1mpid[0m,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1mstate[0m, [1mtime[0m, [1msl[0m, [1mre[0m, [1mpagein[0m, [1mvsz[0m, [1mrss[0m, [1mlim[0m, [1mtsiz[0m, [1m%cpu[0m, [1m%mem[0m, and
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1mcommand[0m.  The [1m-v[0m option implies the [1m-m[0m option.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-w[0m      Use 132 columns to display information, instead of the default
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             which is your window size.  If the [1m-w[0m option is specified more than
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             once, [1mps[0m will use as many columns as necessary without regard for
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             your window size.  When output is not to a terminal, an unlimited
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             number of columns are always used.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-X[0m      When displaying processes matched by other options, skip any
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             processes which do not have a controlling terminal.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-x[0m      When displaying processes matched by other options, include
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             processes which do not have a controlling terminal.  This is the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             opposite of the [1m-X[0m option.  If both [1m-X[0m and [1m-x[0m are specified in the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             same command, then [1mps[0m will use the one which was specified last.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     A complete list of the available keywords is given below.  Some of these
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     keywords are further specified as follows:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m%cpu[0m      The CPU utilization of the process; this is a decaying average
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               over up to a minute of previous (real) time.  Because the time
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               base over which this is computed varies (some processes may be
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               very young), it is possible for the sum of all [1m%cpu[0m fields to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               exceed 100%.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m%mem[0m      The percentage of real memory used by this process.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1mflags[0m     The flags associated with the process as in the include file
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               <[4msys/proc.h[24m>:

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               format.  Otherwise, the start time is displayed using the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               ‚Äú%e%b%y‚Äù format.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1mstate[0m     The state is given by a sequence of characters, for example,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               ‚ÄúRWNA‚Äù.  The first character indicates the run state of the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               process:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               R       Marks a runnable process.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               S       Marks a process that is sleeping for less than about 20
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                       seconds.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               T       Marks a stopped process.

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               Z       Marks a dead process (a ‚Äúzombie‚Äù).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               state information:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                       control terminal.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               <       The process has raised CPU scheduling priority.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               >       The process has specified a soft limit on memory
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                       requirements and is currently exceeding that limit; such
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                       a process is (necessarily) not swapped.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               A       the process has asked for random page replacement
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                       (VA_ANOM, from vadvise(2), for example, lisp(1) in a
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                       garbage collect).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               E       The process is trying to exit.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               L       The process has pages locked in core (for example, for
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                       raw I/O).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               N       The process has reduced CPU scheduling priority (see
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                       setpriority(2)).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               S       The process has asked for FIFO page replacement (VA_SEQL,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                       from vadvise(2), for example, a large image processing
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                       program using virtual memory to sequentially address
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                       voluminous data).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               s       The process is a session leader.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               V       The process is suspended during a vfork(2).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               W       The process is swapped out.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               X       The process is being traced or debugged.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1mtt[0m        An abbreviation for the pathname of the controlling terminal, if
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               any.  The abbreviation consists of the three letters following
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               [4m/dev/tty[24m, or, for the console, ‚Äúcon‚Äù.  This is followed by a ‚Äò-‚Äô
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               if the process can no longer reach that controlling terminal
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               (i.e., it has been revoked).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1mwchan[0m     The event (an address in the system) on which a process waits.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               When printed numerically, the initial part of the address is
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               trimmed off and the result is printed in hex, for example,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               0x80324000 prints as 324000.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     When printing using the command keyword, a process that has exited and has
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     a parent that has not yet waited for the process (in other words, a zombie)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     is listed as ‚Äú<defunct>‚Äù, and a process which is blocked while trying to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     exit is listed as ‚Äú<exiting>‚Äù.  If the arguments cannot be located (usually
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     because it has not been set, as is the case of system processes and/or
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     kernel threads) the command name is printed within square brackets.  The
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     process can change the arguments shown with setproctitle(3).  Otherwise, [1mps[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     makes an educated guess as to the file name and arguments given when the

[?1049h[?1h=KILL(1)                      General Commands Manual                     KILL(1)

[1mNAME[0m
     [1mkill[0m ‚Äì terminate or signal a process

[1mSYNOPSIS[0m
     [1mkill[0m [[1m-s[0m [4msignal_name[24m] [4mpid[24m [4m...[24m
     [1mkill[0m [1m-l[0m [[4mexit_status[24m]
     [1mkill[0m [1m-[0m[4msignal_name[24m [4mpid[24m [4m...[24m
     [1mkill[0m [1m-[0m[4msignal_number[24m [4mpid[24m [4m...[24m

[1mDESCRIPTION[0m
     The [1mkill[0m utility sends a signal to the processes specified by the [4mpid[24m
     operands.

     Only the super-user may send signals to other users' processes.

     The options are as follows:

     [1m-s[0m [4msignal_name[24m
             A symbolic signal name specifying the signal to be sent instead of
             the default TERM.

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-l[0m [[4mexit_status[24m]
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             If no operand is given, list the signal names; otherwise, write the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             signal name corresponding to [4mexit_status[24m.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-[0m[4msignal_name[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             A symbolic signal name specifying the signal to be sent instead of
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             the default TERM.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-[0m[4msignal_number[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             A non-negative decimal integer, specifying the signal to be sent
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             instead of the default TERM.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The following PIDs have special meanings:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     -1      If superuser, broadcast the signal to all processes; otherwise
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             broadcast to all processes belonging to the user.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Some of the more commonly used signals:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     1       HUP (hang up)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     2       INT (interrupt)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     3       QUIT (quit)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     6       ABRT (abort)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     9       KILL (non-catchable, non-ignorable kill)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     14      ALRM (alarm clock)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     15      TERM (software termination signal)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Some shells may provide a builtin [1mkill[0m command which is similar or
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     identical to this utility.  Consult the builtin(1) manual page.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mEXIT[0m [1mSTATUS[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1mkill[0m utility exits¬†0 on success, and¬†>0 if an error occurs.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mEXAMPLES[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Terminate the processes with PIDs 142 and 157:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           kill 142 157
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Send the hangup signal (SIGHUP) to the process with PID 507:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           kill -s HUP 507
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Terminate the process group with PGID 117:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           kill -- -117
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mSEE[0m [1mALSO[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     builtin(1), csh(1), killall(1), ps(1), sh(1), kill(2), sigaction(2)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mSTANDARDS[0m

[?1049h[?1h=GREP(1)                      General Commands Manual                     GREP(1)

[1mNAME[0m
     [1mgrep[0m, [1megrep[0m, [1mfgrep[0m, [1mrgrep[0m, [1mbzgrep[0m, [1mbzegrep[0m, [1mbzfgrep[0m, [1mzgrep[0m, [1mzegrep[0m, [1mzfgrep[0m
     ‚Äì file pattern searcher

[1mSYNOPSIS[0m
     [1mgrep[0m [[1m-abcdDEFGHhIiJLlMmnOopqRSsUVvwXxZz[0m] [[1m-A[0m [4mnum[24m] [[1m-B[0m [4mnum[24m] [[1m-C[0m[[4mnum[24m]]
          [[1m-e[0m [4mpattern[24m] [[1m-f[0m [4mfile[24m] [[1m--binary-files=[0m[4mvalue[24m] [[1m--color[0m[[1m=[0m[4mwhen[24m]]
          [[1m--colour[0m[[1m=[0m[4mwhen[24m]] [[1m--context[0m[[1m=[0m[4mnum[24m]] [[1m--label[0m] [[1m--line-buffered[0m]
          [[1m--null[0m] [[4mpattern[24m] [[4mfile[24m [4m...[24m]

[1mDESCRIPTION[0m
     The [1mgrep[0m utility searches any given input files, selecting lines that match
     one or more patterns.  By default, a pattern matches an input line if the
     regular expression (RE) in the pattern matches the input line without its
     trailing newline.  An empty expression matches every line.  Each input line
     that matches at least one of the patterns is written to the standard
     output.

     [1mgrep[0m is used for simple patterns and basic regular expressions (BREs);
     [1megrep[0m can handle extended regular expressions (EREs).  See re_format(7) for
     more information on regular expressions.  [1mfgrep[0m is quicker than both [1mgrep[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     and [1megrep[0m, but can only handle fixed patterns (i.e., it does not interpret
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     regular expressions).  Patterns may consist of one or more lines, allowing
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     any of the pattern lines to match a portion of the input.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1mzgrep[0m, [1mzegrep[0m, and [1mzfgrep[0m act like [1mgrep[0m, [1megrep[0m, and [1mfgrep[0m, respectively,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     but accept input files compressed with the compress(1) or gzip(1)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     compression utilities.  [1mbzgrep[0m, [1mbzegrep[0m, and [1mbzfgrep[0m act like [1mgrep[0m, [1megrep[0m,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     and [1mfgrep[0m, respectively, but accept input files compressed with the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     bzip2(1) compression utility.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The following options are available:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-A[0m [4mnum[24m, [1m--after-context=[0m[4mnum[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Print [4mnum[24m lines of trailing context after each match.  See also the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1m-B[0m and [1m-C[0m options.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-a[0m, [1m--text[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Treat all files as ASCII text.  Normally [1mgrep[0m will simply print
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             ‚ÄúBinary file ... matches‚Äù if files contain binary characters.  Use
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             of this option forces [1mgrep[0m to output lines matching the specified
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             pattern.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-B[0m [4mnum[24m, [1m--before-context=[0m[4mnum[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Print [4mnum[24m lines of leading context before each match.  See also the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1m-A[0m and [1m-C[0m options.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-b[0m, [1m--byte-offset[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             The offset in bytes of a matched pattern is displayed in front of
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             the respective matched line.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-C[0m[[4mnum[24m], [1m--context[0m[=[4mnum[24m]
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Print [4mnum[24m lines of leading and trailing context surrounding each
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             match.  The default value of [4mnum[24m is ‚Äú2‚Äù and is equivalent to ‚Äú[1m-A[0m [4m2[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1m-B[0m [4m2[24m‚Äù.  Note: no whitespace may be given between the option and its
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             argument.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-c[0m, [1m--count[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Only a count of selected lines is written to standard output.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m--colour=[0m[[4mwhen[24m], [1m--color=[0m[[4mwhen[24m]
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Mark up the matching text with the expression stored in the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             GREP_COLOR environment variable.  The possible values of [4mwhen[24m are
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             ‚Äú[1mnever[0m‚Äù, ‚Äú[1malways[0m‚Äù and ‚Äú[1mauto[0m‚Äù.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-D[0m [4maction[24m, [1m--devices=[0m[4maction[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Specify the demanded [4maction[24m for devices, FIFOs and sockets.  The
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             default [4maction[24m is ‚Äú[1mread[0m‚Äù, which means, that they are read as if
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             they were normal files.  If the [4maction[24m is set to ‚Äú[1mskip[0m‚Äù, devices
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             are silently skipped.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-d[0m [4maction[24m, [1m--directories=[0m[4maction[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Specify the demanded [4maction[24m for directories.  It is ‚Äú[1mread[0m‚Äù by
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             default, which means that the directories are read in the same
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             manner as normal files.  Other possible values are ‚Äú[1mskip[0m‚Äù to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             silently ignore the directories, and ‚Äú[1mrecurse[0m‚Äù to read them
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             recursively, which has the same effect as the [1m-R[0m and [1m-r[0m option.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-E[0m, [1m--extended-regexp[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Interpret [4mpattern[24m as an extended regular expression (i.e., force
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1mgrep[0m to behave as [1megrep[0m).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-e[0m [4mpattern[24m, [1m--regexp=[0m[4mpattern[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Specify a [4mpattern[24m used during the search of the input: an input
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             line is selected if it matches any of the specified patterns.  This
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             option is most useful when multiple [1m-e[0m options are used to specify
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             multiple patterns, or when a [4mpattern[24m begins with a dash (‚Äò-‚Äô).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m--exclude[0m [4mpattern[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             If specified, it excludes files matching the given filename [4mpattern[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             from the search.  Note that [1m--exclude[0m and [1m--include[0m patterns are
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             processed in the order given.  If a name matches multiple patterns,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             the latest matching rule wins.  If no [1m--include[0m pattern is
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             specified, all files are searched that are not excluded.  Patterns
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             are matched to the full path specified, not only to the filename
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             component.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m--exclude-dir[0m [4mpattern[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             If [1m-R[0m is specified, it excludes directories matching the given
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             filename [4mpattern[24m from the search.  Note that [1m--exclude-dir[0m and
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1m--include-dir[0m patterns are processed in the order given.  If a name
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             matches multiple patterns, the latest matching rule wins.  If no
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1m--include-dir[0m pattern is specified, all directories are searched
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             that are not excluded.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-F[0m, [1m--fixed-strings[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Interpret [4mpattern[24m as a set of fixed strings (i.e., force [1mgrep[0m to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             behave as [1mfgrep[0m).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-f[0m [4mfile[24m, [1m--file=[0m[4mfile[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Read one or more newline separated patterns from [4mfile[24m.  Empty
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             pattern lines match every input line.  Newlines are not considered
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             part of a pattern.  If [4mfile[24m is empty, nothing is matched.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-G[0m, [1m--basic-regexp[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Interpret [4mpattern[24m as a basic regular expression (i.e., force [1mgrep[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             to behave as traditional [1mgrep[0m).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-H[0m      Always print filename headers with output lines.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-h[0m, [1m--no-filename[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Never print filename headers (i.e., filenames) with output lines.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m--help[0m  Print a brief help message.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-I[0m      Ignore binary files.  This option is equivalent to the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             ‚Äú[1m--binary-file=without-match[0m‚Äù option.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-i[0m, [1m--ignore-case[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Perform case insensitive matching.  By default, [1mgrep[0m is case
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             sensitive.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m--include[0m [4mpattern[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             If specified, only files matching the given filename [4mpattern[24m are
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             searched.  Note that [1m--include[0m and [1m--exclude[0m patterns are processed
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             in the order given.  If a name matches multiple patterns, the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             latest matching rule wins.  Patterns are matched to the full path
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             specified, not only to the filename component.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m--include-dir[0m [4mpattern[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             If [1m-R[0m is specified, only directories matching the given filename
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [4mpattern[24m are searched.  Note that [1m--include-dir[0m and [1m--exclude-dir[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             patterns are processed in the order given.  If a name matches
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             multiple patterns, the latest matching rule wins.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-J[0m, [1m--bz2decompress[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Decompress the bzip2(1) compressed file before looking for the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             text.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-L[0m, [1m--files-without-match[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Only the names of files not containing selected lines are written
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             to standard output.  Pathnames are listed once per file searched.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             If the standard input is searched, the string ‚Äú(standard input)‚Äù is
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             written unless a [1m--label[0m is specified.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-l[0m, [1m--files-with-matches[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Only the names of files containing selected lines are written to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             standard output.  [1mgrep[0m will only search a file until a match has
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             been found, making searches potentially less expensive.  Pathnames
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             are listed once per file searched.  If the standard input is
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             searched, the string ‚Äú(standard input)‚Äù is written unless a [1m--label[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             is specified.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m--label[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Label to use in place of ‚Äú(standard input)‚Äù for a file name where a
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             file name would normally be printed.  This option applies to [1m-H[0m,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             [1m-L[0m, and [1m-l[0m.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m--mmap[0m  Use mmap(2) instead of read(2) to read input, which can result in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             better performance under some circumstances but can cause undefined
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             behaviour.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-M[0m, [1m--lzma[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Decompress the LZMA compressed file before looking for the text.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-m[0m [4mnum[24m, [1m--max-count=[0m[4mnum[24m

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-n[0m, [1m--line-number[0m

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             each file processed.  This option is ignored if [1m-c[0m, [1m-L[0m, [1m-l[0m, or [1m-q[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             is specified.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m--null[0m  Prints a zero-byte after the file name.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-O[0m      If [1m-R[0m is specified, follow symbolic links only if they were
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             explicitly listed on the command line.  The default is not to

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-o[0m, [1m--only-matching[0m

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1mgrep[0m utility is compliant with the IEEE Std 1003.1-2008 (‚ÄúPOSIX.1‚Äù)

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     the behaviour of the [1m-f[0m flag when used with an empty pattern file is left
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     undefined.

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Historic versions of the [1mgrep[0m utility also supported the flags [[1m-ruy[0m].
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     This implementation supports those options; however, their use is strongly
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     discouraged.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mHISTORY[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1mgrep[0m command first appeared in Version¬†6 AT&T UNIX.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mBUGS[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1mgrep[0m utility does not normalize Unicode input, so a pattern containing
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     composed characters will not match decomposed input, and vice versa.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[KmacOS 12.5                       March 22, 2021                       macOS 12.5
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[K[7m(END)[27m[K[K[?1l>[?1049l[1m[7m%[27m[1m[0m [?1049h[?1h=LN(1)                        General Commands Manual                       LN(1)

[1mNAME[0m
     [1mln[0m, [1mlink[0m ‚Äì link files

[1mSYNOPSIS[0m
     [1mln[0m [[1m-L[0m | [1m-P[0m | [1m-s[0m [[1m-F[0m]] [[1m-f[0m | [1m-iw[0m] [[1m-hnv[0m] [4msource_file[24m [[4mtarget_file[24m]
     [1mln[0m [[1m-L[0m | [1m-P[0m | [1m-s[0m [[1m-F[0m]] [[1m-f[0m | [1m-iw[0m] [[1m-hnv[0m] [4msource_file[24m [4m...[24m [4mtarget_dir[24m
     [1mlink[0m [4msource_file[24m [4mtarget_file[24m

[1mDESCRIPTION[0m
     The [1mln[0m utility creates a new directory entry (linked file) for the file
     name specified by [4mtarget_file[24m.  The [4mtarget_file[24m will be created with the
     same file modes as the [4msource_file[24m.  It is useful for maintaining multiple
     copies of a file in many places at once without using up storage for the
     ‚Äúcopies‚Äù; instead, a link ‚Äúpoints‚Äù to the original copy.  There are two
     types of links; hard links and symbolic links.  How a link ‚Äúpoints‚Äù to a
     file is one of the differences between a hard and symbolic link.

     The options are as follows:

     [1m-F[0m    If the target file already exists and is a directory, then remove it
           so that the link may occur.  The [1m-F[0m option should be used with either
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           [1m-f[0m or [1m-i[0m options.  If neither [1m-f[0m nor [1m-i[0m is specified, [1m-f[0m is implied.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           The [1m-F[0m option is a no-op unless [1m-s[0m is specified.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-L[0m    When creating a hard link to a symbolic link, create a hard link to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           the target of the symbolic link.  This is the default.  This option
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           cancels the [1m-P[0m option.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-P[0m    When creating a hard link to a symbolic link, create a hard link to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           the symbolic link itself.  This option cancels the [1m-L[0m option.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-f[0m    If the target file already exists, then unlink it so that the link
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           may occur.  (The [1m-f[0m option overrides any previous [1m-i[0m and [1m-w[0m options.)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-h[0m    If the [4mtarget_file[24m or [4mtarget_dir[24m is a symbolic link, do not follow
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           it.  This is most useful with the [1m-f[0m option, to replace a symlink
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           which may point to a directory.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-i[0m    Cause [1mln[0m to write a prompt to standard error if the target file
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           exists.  If the response from the standard input begins with the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           character ‚Äòy‚Äô or ‚ÄòY‚Äô, then unlink the target file so that the link
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           may occur.  Otherwise, do not attempt the link.  (The [1m-i[0m option
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           overrides any previous [1m-f[0m options.)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-n[0m    Same as [1m-h[0m, for compatibility with other [1mln[0m implementations.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-s[0m    Create a symbolic link.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-v[0m    Cause [1mln[0m to be verbose, showing files as they are processed.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-w[0m    Warn if the source of a symbolic link does not currently exist.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     By default, [1mln[0m makes [4mhard[24m links.  A hard link to a file is
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     indistinguishable from the original directory entry; any changes to a file
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           the symbolic link itself.  This option cancels the [1m-L[0m option.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     [1m-P[0m    When creating a hard link to a symbolic link, create a hard link to
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     By default, [1mln[0m makes [4mhard[24m links.  A hard link to a file is
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     indistinguishable from the original directory entry; any changes to a file
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     are effectively independent of the name used to reference the file.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Directories may not be hardlinked, and hard links may not span file
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     systems.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     A symbolic link contains the name of the file to which it is linked.  The
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     referenced file is used when an open(2) operation is performed on the link.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     A stat(2) on a symbolic link will return the linked-to file; an lstat(2)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     must be done to obtain information about the link.  The readlink(2) call
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     may be used to read the contents of a symbolic link.  Symbolic links may
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     span file systems and may refer to directories.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Given one or two arguments, [1mln[0m creates a link to an existing file
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [4msource_file[24m.  If [4mtarget_file[24m is given, the link has that name; [4mtarget_file[24m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     may also be a directory in which to place the link; otherwise it is placed
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     in the current directory.  If only the directory is specified, the link
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     will be made to the last component of [4msource_file[24m.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Given more than two arguments, [1mln[0m makes links in [4mtarget_dir[24m to all the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     named source files.  The links made will have the same name as the files
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     being linked to.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     When the utility is called as [1mlink[0m, exactly two arguments must be supplied,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     neither of which may specify a directory.  No options may be supplied in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     this simple mode of operation, which performs a link(2) operation using the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     two passed arguments.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mEXAMPLES[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Create a symbolic link named [4m/home/src[24m and point it to [4m/usr/src[24m:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           # ln -s /usr/src /home/src
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Hard link [4m/usr/local/bin/fooprog[24m to file [4m/usr/local/bin/fooprog-1.0[24m:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           # ln /usr/local/bin/fooprog-1.0 /usr/local/bin/fooprog
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     As an exercise, try the following commands:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           # ls -i /bin/[
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           11553 /bin/[
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           # ls -i /bin/test
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           11553 /bin/test
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Note that both files have the same inode; that is, [4m/bin/[[24m is essentially an
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     alias for the test(1) command.  This hard link exists so test(1) may be
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     invoked from shell scripts, for example, using the if [ ] construct.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     In the next example, the second call to [1mln[0m removes the original [4mfoo[24m and
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     creates a replacement pointing to [4mbaz[24m:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           # mkdir bar baz
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           # ln -s bar foo
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           # ln -shf baz foo
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Without the [1m-h[0m option, this would instead leave [4mfoo[24m pointing to [4mbar[24m and
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     inside [4mfoo[24m create a new symlink [4mbaz[24m pointing to itself.  This results from
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     directory-walking.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     An easy rule to remember is that the argument order for [1mln[0m is the same as
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     for cp(1): The first argument needs to exist, the second one is created.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mCOMPATIBILITY[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1m-h[0m, [1m-i[0m, [1m-n[0m, [1m-v[0m and [1m-w[0m options are non-standard and their use in scripts
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     is not recommended.  They are provided solely for compatibility with other
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1mln[0m implementations.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1m-F[0m option is a FreeBSD extension and should not be used in portable
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     scripts.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mSEE[0m [1mALSO[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     link(2), lstat(2), readlink(2), stat(2), symlink(2), symlink(7)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mSTANDARDS[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The [1mln[0m utility conforms to IEEE Std 1003.2-1992 (‚ÄúPOSIX.2‚Äù).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     The simplified [1mlink[0m command conforms to Version¬†2 of the Single UNIX
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Specification (‚ÄúSUSv2‚Äù).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[1mHISTORY[0m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     inside [4mfoo[24m create a new symlink [4mbaz[24m pointing to itself.  This results from
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     Without the [1m-h[0m option, this would instead leave [4mfoo[24m pointing to [4mbar[24m and
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           # ln -shf baz foo
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           # ln -s bar foo
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           # mkdir bar baz
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     creates a replacement pointing to [4mbaz[24m:
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     In the next example, the second call to [1mln[0m removes the original [4mfoo[24m and
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     invoked from shell scripts, for example, using the if [ ] construct.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     alias for the test(1) command.  This hard link exists so test(1) may be
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     Note that both files have the same inode; that is, [4m/bin/[[24m is essentially an
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           11553 /bin/test
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           # ls -i /bin/test
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           11553 /bin/[
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           # ls -i /bin/[
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     As an exercise, try the following commands:
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           # ln /usr/local/bin/fooprog-1.0 /usr/local/bin/fooprog
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     Hard link [4m/usr/local/bin/fooprog[24m to file [4m/usr/local/bin/fooprog-1.0[24m:
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM           # ln -s /usr/src /home/src
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     Create a symbolic link named [4m/home/src[24m and point it to [4m/usr/src[24m:
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM[1mEXAMPLES[0m
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     two passed arguments.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     this simple mode of operation, which performs a link(2) operation using the
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     neither of which may specify a directory.  No options may be supplied in
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     When the utility is called as [1mlink[0m, exactly two arguments must be supplied,
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     being linked to.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     named source files.  The links made will have the same name as the files
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     Given more than two arguments, [1mln[0m makes links in [4mtarget_dir[24m to all the
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     will be made to the last component of [4msource_file[24m.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     in the current directory.  If only the directory is specified, the link
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     may also be a directory in which to place the link; otherwise it is placed
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     [4msource_file[24m.  If [4mtarget_file[24m is given, the link has that name; [4mtarget_file[24m
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     Given one or two arguments, [1mln[0m creates a link to an existing file
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM     span file systems and may refer to directories.
[24;1H[K:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           # ln /usr/local/bin/fooprog-1.0 /usr/local/bin/fooprog
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     As an exercise, try the following commands:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           # ls -i /bin/[
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           11553 /bin/[
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           # ls -i /bin/test
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           11553 /bin/test
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     Note that both files have the same inode; that is, [4m/bin/[[24m is essentially an
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     alias for the test(1) command.  This hard link exists so test(1) may be
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     invoked from shell scripts, for example, using the if [ ] construct.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     In the next example, the second call to [1mln[0m removes the original [4mfoo[24m and

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
